### Question 97: I'm having some bad experience with a professor teaching a course. The problem was his way of delivering does not meet academic standard and I want to say something about this with people having higher authorities. What should I do?  
### Answer: 

First, discuss the matter with the course instructor(s) to try and resolve the issue. If the problem remains unresolved, you should follow the university's established procedure for appealing a final grade. This typically involves submitting a Review of Final Grade Request form to the Registrar's Office within five business days from the date the final grade is posted. The Registrar's Office will then inform the Dean’s Office of the case. If the Deans cannot mediate the issue, the Registrar's Office will organize a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter.

The references provided are relevant to the question as they outline the specific steps a student should take to address concerns about a professor's teaching methods and to appeal a final grade if necessary. The context provided includes the university's policies on academic appeals, which directly address the situation you're describing. It's important to follow these steps in a timely manner and to gather any relevant documentation to support your case.

In addition, if the issue is more about the professor's teaching methods and not directly related to a grade dispute, you might also consider:

- Seeking advice from the Office of the Dean of Students or the Academic Advising Center for guidance on how to address the issue.
- Writing a formal letter to the department chair or the head of the academic department expressing your concerns and requesting a meeting to discuss the situation.
- If the professor's teaching methods are affecting your academic performance significantly, you might also consider discussing this with the academic advisor or the Office of Student Success for further support.

Remember, it's important to approach the situation professionally and to document all interactions and communications related to the issue.  

<details>  
<summary>References</summary>  

[Source: Academic-Policy_V5.1.pdf, Page: 10]

Otherwise, the Registrar's Office organizes a panel review with the Dean’s Office for an independent evaluation of the grade. The grade determined after this evaluation shall be the final grade. In cases concerning the interpretation of a course policy, the Dean’s Office will defer to the course syllabus whenever possible and otherwise will make a final ruling on the matter.

An Academic Warning is sent out by the Registrar’s Office. ### Question 98: I'm a third year student and don't know if I should do a capstone project then where should I go to get advice?  
### Answer: 

Your primary advisor may not be an expert on your chosen subject, but they are there to guide you through the research process and evaluate your mastery of it. If you feel you need expert guidance on a specific topic, consider requesting an external secondary advisor who does specialize in that area. Alternatively, propose a Capstone project based on a 300-level research seminar you've taken, or ask faculty for topic suggestions. This way, you're more likely to end up with a primary advisor who is also a subject-matter expert. Remember, the Capstone project is a year-long commitment and should be considered if you enjoy historical research and want to undertake a long-term project. However, if you don't particularly enjoy independent research and wish to graduate with distinction, focusing on GPA honors might be a better option. The Capstone sequence typically starts in the Fall with Capstone I, where you'll refine your project proposal, secure resources, and do preliminary work. Changes to your topic are possible but require careful consideration and approval from your primary advisor. Always clarify what is required at each stage of the project with your advisor to ensure you're on the right track. Remember, the goal is for you to do the thinking and working, not for your advisor to do it for you.

Your primary advisor may not be an expert on your chosen subject and almost certainly isn’t an expert on the narrow historical problem you will tackle in your Capstone project—and that is okay! The main role of your Capstone advisor is to guide you through the research process and to evaluate your mastery of that process, regardless of the topic. If you feel that you need expert guidance on a particular topic and that no one on our faculty has specialized knowledge on that topic, you may want to consider requesting an external secondary advisor who does. Another way to approach this is to propose a Capstone project based on a 300-level research seminar that you have taken at Fulbright, or to ask the faculty for topic suggestions—that way, you are more likely to end up with a primary advisor who is also a subject-matter expert! The Capstone project is a year-long undertaking with less structure than a traditional course. It is certainly not the easiest way to complete your degree, and it may not be the most logical option for you, depending on your interests and your post-graduation plans. You should not consider it to be the default pathway to finishing your degree. One of the best reasons to undertake a Capstone project is if you enjoy doing historical research (which you will have sampled in Hands-On History and the research seminars you have completed) and want an opportunity to carry out a long-term research project. For such students, the Capstone year provides time and guidance that is unparalleled by any course or other opportunity at the undergraduate level. However, if you wish to graduate with distinction—an honorable goal— but you don’t particularly enjoy doing independent research, you may want to skip the Capstone and focus on GPA honors instead! ### Question 99: I'm a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and going to attend a tournament. I need the official transcript and asking for some absence in classes then where should I get help?  
### Answer: 

If you are a member of Fulbright Basketball Club and need to attend a tournament, you should follow the university's procedure for requesting an excused absence due to university-sponsored events. Here's how you should proceed:

1. **Contact Faculty/Supervising Staff**: First, inform your faculty or supervising staff about your upcoming absence. They are responsible for requesting an Excused Absence form on your behalf.

2. **University Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form**: Your faculty or supervising staff should fill out the University Official Activity Excused Absence Request Form. This form is submitted to the Dean’s Office, with copies (cc) to the Academic Affairs and Registrar’s Office for record-keeping.

3. **Check Academic Standing**: Before completing the form, your faculty or supervising staff should confirm your academic standing with the Registrar’s Office to ensure you are in good standing and not on probation.

4. **Submit Documentation**: Ensure that you provide any necessary documentation related to the tournament, such as tournament schedules, letters of invitation, or any other relevant paperwork.

5. **Contact Instructors**: It is your responsibility to contact your instructors to discuss making up any missed work.

6. **Registrar’s Office and Academic Affairs**: Keep in touch with the Registrar’s Office and Academic Affairs to ensure that all necessary steps are followed and your absence is properly documented.

7. **Official Transcript**: For the official transcript, you should contact the Registrar’s Office directly. They can guide you on the process for obtaining an official transcript, which typically involves submitting a request form and possibly a fee.

8. **Financial Considerations**: If your absence affects your financial aid or tuition payments, it would be wise to check in with the Student Financial Services team to discuss any potential impacts and explore any available solutions.

9. **Emergency Contact**: In case of an emergency or if you are unable to follow these steps due to unforeseen circumstances, contact the Academic Affairs team or Registrar’s Office during business hours.

By following these steps, you should be able to manage your absence for the tournament and obtain your official transcript when needed. Remember to communicate clearly and promptly with all involved parties to ensure a smooth process.

### Question 101: How can I borrow books from the library?  
### Answer: 

You can borrow books from the library by following these steps:

1. Visit the library: Go to the library and locate the section where books are kept.

2. Search for books: Use the library catalog or the librarian to find the books you need for your research.

3. Check availability: Confirm that the books you want are available and not on loan to someone else.

4. Borrow books: Present your student ID or library card to the librarian or at the self-checkout machine to borrow the books.

5. Note due dates: Write down or remember the due dates for returning the books.

6. Return books on time: Make sure to return the books by the due date to avoid late fees.

Remember to respect the library's rules and policies regarding borrowing limits and renewals. If you need help finding books or have any questions, don't hesitate to ask the library staff for assistance.

### Question 102: How to work with major report?  
### Answer: 

To work effectively on a major report for a Capstone project, follow these steps:

1. **Define Clear Objectives**: Start by defining clear and achievable objectives for your project. This will guide your research and writing process.

2. **Conduct a Thorough Literature Review**: Dive into a comprehensive literature review to understand the context, existing solutions, and gaps in the current research. This will help you position your project and identify a unique angle.

3. **Develop a Detailed Project Plan and Timeline**: Create a detailed project plan and timeline for Capstone 2. This plan should outline the steps you will take, including the methods you will use, the timeline for each phase of the project, and milestones to track your progress.

4. **Structure Your Report**: Organize your report according to the submission requirements, which typically include an Introduction/Motivation, Literature Review, Problem Statement/Description, and Proposed Methods, Plan, and Timeline for Capstone 2.

5. **Regular Communication with Advisors**: Keep open lines of communication with your primary and secondary advisors. Share early drafts, discuss your progress, and seek feedback regularly. This will help you stay on track and make necessary adjustments to your project.

6. **Follow Submission Guidelines**: Adhere strictly to the submission guidelines, including deadlines and formatting requirements. Ensure your report is well-structured, well-researched, and professionally presented.

7. **Engage with Your Secondary Advisor**: If you have a secondary advisor, especially for applied and creative projects, work closely with them to incorporate their expertise and feedback into your work.

8. **Prepare for Evaluation**: Understand the expectations for the Evaluation Report, which includes the intellectual rationale, goals, evaluation questions, and insights or recommendations for applied action or future inquiry.

9. **Stay Organized and Manage Your Time**: Keep a steady work ethic, manage your time effectively, and stay organized. Regularly review your timeline and adjust as necessary to meet your objectives.

10. **Seek Feedback and Revision**: Be open to feedback and be prepared to revise your work. This iterative process is crucial for improving the quality of your report and project.

By following these steps, you can work effectively on your major report, ensuring a well-structured, well-researched, and professionally presented project that meets the expectations of your Capstone course.

### Question 103: How many way can I fill in the requirements of EL?  
### Answer: 

For Class of 2024 students, they need to complete 16 credits (4 courses) to fulfill their Exploratory requirements, one course from each category (E1-Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, E3- Sciences and Engineering, and E4-Mathematics and Computing), with at most 4 out of 16 credits counted as Pass/No Pass. For students of classes of 2025, 2026, and 2027, they need to complete 32 credits (8 courses), eight credits from each category, to fulfill their Exploratory requirements.

Students need to complete 8 credits (2 courses at the 100-level or 200-level) chosen from each of the three categories: E1- Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, and STEM. No course can be taken to fulﬁll more than one category. At most, 8 exploratory credits can be taken as Pass/No Pass. Up to two 8 exploratory credits (2 courses) can be counted towards the student’s major requirements. If a student has more than one major, the 8-credit limit is independently applied to each major. Students should aim to complete the Exploratory requirements by the end of their second year. Notes: •  Class of 2023 students are exempted from the Exploratory requirements. • There are four exploratory categories for the students of classes of 2024, 2025, 2026, and 2027: E1-Arts and Humanities, E2-Social Sciences, E3- Sciences and Engineering, and E4-Mathematics and Computing. • Class of 2024 students need to complete 16 credits (4 courses) to fulﬁll their
